<div id="review_189633579" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/189633579" />
    <a title="Samantha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5880552-samantha"><img alt="Samantha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493644616p2/5880552.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/189633579?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha" href="/user/show/5880552-samantha">Samantha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5880552-samantha?shelf=own-it">own-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5880552-samantha?shelf=british-history">british-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5880552-samantha?shelf=plantagenets">plantagenets</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5880552-samantha?shelf=more-historical-than-fiction">more-historical-than-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5880552-samantha?shelf=seriously-read-this">seriously-read-this</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer189633579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2292945394511538248">Sometimes I have a difficult time deciding how to rate a book. I expect to find that a 5-star book stands out among the millions of written pages out there. This one does. I have read it before and knew exactly what would happen, but that didn't stop tears from forming in my eyes at times as Penman skillfully made history come alive.<br/><br/>Even the title is more eye-catching and thought provoking than most. <i>When Christ and His Saints Slept</i> was an era of English history fraught with unfortunate events b</span>
  <span id="freeText2292945394511538248" style="display:none">Sometimes I have a difficult time deciding how to rate a book. I expect to find that a 5-star book stands out among the millions of written pages out there. This one does. I have read it before and knew exactly what would happen, but that didn't stop tears from forming in my eyes at times as Penman skillfully made history come alive.<br /><br />Even the title is more eye-catching and thought provoking than most. <i>When Christ and His Saints Slept</i> was an era of English history fraught with unfortunate events beginning with the sinking of the White Ship in 1120. Henry I, who had managed to sire at least 20 illegitimate children, had only one legitimate male heir. William was expected to be England's next king until he got on board the beautiful but doomed vessel. <br /><br />Henry I makes his daughter Maude (Matilda) his heir in one of the worst considered last testaments of all time and throws England into a 20 year civil war so bloody and tormented that it was believed that Christ and His saints slept. Maude intends to fight for the crown that few believe any woman should wear, and is shocked when her cousin, Stephen of Blois, is the one to steal it from her.<br /><br />Enough of restating history, you can find the details of the struggles between Maude and Stephen easily enough. What you will not find is a telling of their lives that is as detailed, moving, and well-written as Penman's. The cast of characters in this novel is amazingly large, but developed well enough that the reader can track them as though they are friends (or enemies). The rich detail of scenery, battles, and historical detail is second to none. The reader will learn as much as if reading non-fiction, while at the same time be entertained by the personalities, humor, and just a little bit of romance. No other author creates a whole world as realistically as Sharon Kay Penman. She is in a league of her own. The reader can sympathize with Maude and cry for Stephen and not find any reason why that should not be so. Picking sides is as difficult for those reading their story now as it was for their nobles those many years ago.<br /><br />After the back and forth, years of sacrifice and struggle, this installment concludes with the ascendancy of Henry II. He seems like the golden savior of England, and I was almost brought to tears again seeing the beginning of his rule so full of hope and knowing how it is to end. His and Eleanor's story is just beginning when this novel ends, but is continued in the next volume, Time and Chance. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2292945394511538248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1217617991" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1217617991" />
    <a title="Deborah Pickstone" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37849334-deborah-pickstone"><img alt="Deborah Pickstone" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1432503842p2/37849334.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1217617991?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Pickstone" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Pickstone" href="/user/show/37849334-deborah-pickstone">Deborah Pickstone</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37849334-deborah-pickstone?shelf=favourite-authors">favourite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37849334-deborah-pickstone?shelf=serieses-fictional">serieses-fictional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37849334-deborah-pickstone?shelf=makes-me-think">makes-me-think</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37849334-deborah-pickstone?shelf=myth-and-legend">myth-and-legend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37849334-deborah-pickstone?shelf=re-reads">re-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37849334-deborah-pickstone?shelf=medieval">medieval</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37849334-deborah-pickstone?shelf=ethical-issues">ethical-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37849334-deborah-pickstone?shelf=human-nature">human-nature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37849334-deborah-pickstone?shelf=uk-fiction">uk-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37849334-deborah-pickstone?shelf=lets-be-pacifists">lets-be-pacifists</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1217617991" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2000588840577373284">I have read this several times but realised during this re-read how much more critical a reader I have become - not necessarily a good thing, in some ways. So, the complaint first; writing forsoothly. I wish she wouldn't. Also, the use of the term 'lad/lass' every time someone speaks to someone else gets REALLY irritating. I know it's an English habit but not everyone uses it and I doubt it was different then. It's part of the writing forsoothly. I think it's one of the dangers of writing about </span>
  <span id="freeText2000588840577373284" style="display:none">I have read this several times but realised during this re-read how much more critical a reader I have become - not necessarily a good thing, in some ways. So, the complaint first; writing forsoothly. I wish she wouldn't. Also, the use of the term 'lad/lass' every time someone speaks to someone else gets REALLY irritating. I know it's an English habit but not everyone uses it and I doubt it was different then. It's part of the writing forsoothly. I think it's one of the dangers of writing about English history in the US.<br /><br />My gripe being over, this is probably the best biographical novel there is about this short and harrowing era of English history. For the most part the history is sound and well-researched. Ms Penman only falls down on the sort of detail that can slide past the eye - buying a tablecloth at the market to go for a picnic, for instance. I am no expert in the history of tablecloths and their use. While they were in use in that time, the sort of table that would have worn one would have demanded a very large one. Your tablecloth's job would have been to announce 'I have lots of money' and was not something you'd expect to find on a picnic - not one where adultery was the main course, anyway! Perhaps he could have bought a horse blanket? Oh, just call me Miss Picky!<br /><br />This is a long book and for me it reads fast! I find the Anarchy an especially fascinating period, peopled by some characters who are truly unbelievable. There are almost no invented characters in this story - just one of the main cast and a few supporting cast - and <i>no-one</i> could have made up Stephen; a new man, a dreamer, humane and chivalrous and yet a much respected warrior, so long as he wasn't involved in anything that went on for too long or he'd wander off and find something more interesting to do - making anyone under siege by him not very worried at all! The most fascinating and least well-known character in the story is his wife, Matilda, who <i>could</i> besiege and stick with it and who captured Robert of Gloucester, thus redeeming Stephen from imprisonment and the end of his reign.<br /><br />We get to Eleanor of Aquitaine toward the end but I am not as beglamoured by her as people seem to be. Unsurprisingly, Henry, child of that shrinking violet the Empress Maude, found himself a woman of strong personality to marry - and to fall out with, eventually. Henry is <i>the</i> personality of this era and this look at his formative years is most interesting.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2000588840577373284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2726793412" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2726793412" />
    <a title="Steve Donoghue" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2209747-steve-donoghue"><img alt="Steve Donoghue" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357079972p2/2209747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2726793412?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve Donoghue" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve Donoghue" href="/user/show/2209747-steve-donoghue">Steve Donoghue</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2209747-steve-donoghue?shelf=older-books">older-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2726793412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15091925615006754592">Well! My first impression, back when this book appeared in 1995, was that it ran aground on all the author's research and failed really to ignite as a big sprawling work of fiction. But now, returning to the book a quarter-century later, I saw SO much more of its merits. In some very real sense, this could be viewed as a work of dramatized history rather than historicized drama - it's fantastic and well-paced and genuinely empathetic throughout. So glad I re-visited this one.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1622758701" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1622758701" />

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11269263-james-burns?shelf=my-librairy">my-librairy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1622758701" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6286100941754702941"> I have always loved historical books about Eleanor of Aquitaine and Henry II, and even though this a work Historical Fiction it was well researched and meets my criteria for Historical Novels. 1st, is it historical accurate describing Battles, and Characters. 2nd, are the characters described real people and how many fictional people are there. 3rd, Can the book come to life as if I'm living the story.<br/> I don't have the words to describe how much I enjoyed reading this book. <br/> The first chapters </span>
  <span id="freeText6286100941754702941" style="display:none"> I have always loved historical books about Eleanor of Aquitaine and Henry II, and even though this a work Historical Fiction it was well researched and meets my criteria for Historical Novels. 1st, is it historical accurate describing Battles, and Characters. 2nd, are the characters described real people and how many fictional people are there. 3rd, Can the book come to life as if I'm living the story.<br /> I don't have the words to describe how much I enjoyed reading this book. <br /> The first chapters is about, Henry I, and the death of his only male heir by drowning when the ship he was on crossing the English Channel,before his death , he named his daughter Maude (Matilda) as heir to the throne, and made all the Barons and titled men, swear an oath of fealty. After hearing about the death of the king, His nephew Stephen usurped the throne,while his cousin and lawful heir, was in the Duchy of Normandy. King Stephen had all the Lords and Barons swear an oath of fealty to him. The King, the Barons and lords justified their breaking their oath of fealty to Maude, stating that the Oath was not valid because it was made under duress. So begins a bloody Civil war for the crown of England, finally it was settled after the death of the Kings oldest son, King Stephen and Henry II came to terms. Stephen would remain King as long as he lived, and adopted Henry and named him, heir to the throne.<br /> Eleanor of Aquitaine, played a substantial role in this story and history, Eleanor was the Queen consort of France.The Marriage of Eleanor and King Louis of France was annulled do to the fact that they were Cousins and was illegally married. <br /> I always try not to spoil the book by giving to much information.There are two events in this book, that I have tell. the first event made me laugh so hard that I cried, and the second event made me cry at the death of Robert and Maud's half brother born out of wedlock. One of the injustice in English history was not named his fathers heir, in my opinion, he would of made far better Ruler than either Stephen.<br /> The 1st event was when Henry invaded England at 14, hiring mercenaries, after suffering a couples losses, he could not afford to pay his men and they were getting restless. Maude Sent Ranulf ( a fictional Character) her half brother to try an convince him to return back to Normandy at that she would give money for him to pay his soldiers. when Ranulf broached The subject Henry told him he had the money. of course his uncle was curious where he got the money, he asked him if he was getting it by illegal means. and he was taken by surprised when Henry had Wrote his cousin, King Stephen for the money.<br /> The 2nd event was the death of Robert, half brother to Matilda, his death was so touching, that I couldn't help but cry, I was half expecting to read, here lies the greatest knight of all. Robert was a true Knight in the sense of Arthur's Knights of the round table.<br /> I Highly recommend this book . This was Sharon Kaye Penman at her best. </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer574976310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4991622824002623642">Christ and his saints slept because they read this book.<br/><br/>There's too much exposition and too little action. The characters spend most of their time playing the "as you know, Bob" game. Very little happens "on stage"; most important events are revealed in letters that are read out to the amazement and shock of all present. Characters are too farsighted at times, having an unrealistic ability to foresee all the repercussions of an event.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3421123073" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Regan Walker" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7363897-regan-walker"><img alt="Regan Walker" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442636914p2/7363897.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3421123073?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Regan Walker" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Regan Walker" href="/user/show/7363897-regan-walker">Regan Walker</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7363897-regan-walker?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7363897-regan-walker?shelf=12th-century">12th-century</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3421123073" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13324386458770030111">4 and ½ Stars! History of 12th Century England Brought to Life<br/><br/>This story of England and France in the time of the Civil War between Stephen and the Empress Maude begins in 1135 A.D. and continues to 1154 A.D. As King Henry I dies, his barons faced the unwelcome prospect of being ruled either by Henry's beautiful daughter, Maude, Countess of Anjou, or her cousin Stephen, a great battle commander but a weak statesman. The Civil War that resulted from their struggle for the Crown was to wreak havoc</span>
  <span id="freeText13324386458770030111" style="display:none">4 and ½ Stars! History of 12th Century England Brought to Life<br /><br />This story of England and France in the time of the Civil War between Stephen and the Empress Maude begins in 1135 A.D. and continues to 1154 A.D. As King Henry I dies, his barons faced the unwelcome prospect of being ruled either by Henry's beautiful daughter, Maude, Countess of Anjou, or her cousin Stephen, a great battle commander but a weak statesman. The Civil War that resulted from their struggle for the Crown was to wreak havoc on England and the lives of the common people as barons switched sides time and again.<br /><br />Penman's novel is like diving into that time in the past. Most of the characters are real and those who are fictional will seem real to the reader. She weaves a splendid tapestry of medieval life and tragedy, even as the way is prepared for Henry II and Eleanor of Aquitaine and the Plantagenets.<br /><br />Long at 738 pages, one has to love the history to linger so long in a novel. It seemed to me to get more exciting and more interesting as it went along, especially when young Henry fitz Empress shows up and we meet the delightful, smart and beautiful Eleanor of Aquitaine. Recommended for the lover of historical fiction (which I am).<br /><br />The Henry II and Eleanor of Aquitaine series:<br /><br />When Christ and His Saints Slept<br />Time and Chance<br />Devil’s Brood</span>
  <a data-text-id="13324386458770030111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2887886157" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2887886157" />
    <a title="Pam Baddeley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42764850-pam-baddeley"><img alt="Pam Baddeley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442488147p2/42764850.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2887886157?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pam Baddeley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pam Baddeley" href="/user/show/42764850-pam-baddeley">Pam Baddeley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140166361" href="/book/show/433074.When_Christ_and_His_Saints_Slept">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42764850-pam-baddeley?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2887886157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1832313741141072174">I have meant for some years to read this author's long novel about Richard III, so when this one instead appeared in a charity shop was tempted. I didn't know much about the period it covers other than remembering that the war between King Stephen and Empress/would-be Queen Maude (aka Matilda) forms the background to the Cadfael series by Ellis Peters.<br/><br/>I enjoyed this book in parts, principally when the scenes developed naturally with some nice interaction between historical characters such as Hen</span>
  <span id="freeText1832313741141072174" style="display:none">I have meant for some years to read this author's long novel about Richard III, so when this one instead appeared in a charity shop was tempted. I didn't know much about the period it covers other than remembering that the war between King Stephen and Empress/would-be Queen Maude (aka Matilda) forms the background to the Cadfael series by Ellis Peters.<br /><br />I enjoyed this book in parts, principally when the scenes developed naturally with some nice interaction between historical characters such as Henry, future King, and Eleanor of Aquitaine. And the book was educational as I certainly know more about the period than beforehand. I wasn't so keen on the huge chunk that revolved around the imaginary character Ranulf and his friends/relations and his strung out hopeless love affair. I can see the point of putting such a character in scenes to interact with the real historical characters, to give a third party onlooker with whom the reader can identify and who can perhaps help to convey key facts, but there were extended interludes based around this character's misadventures elsewhere. I felt that the section in Wales was put in to allow the author to display her research about medieval Welsh society. In an already very long book, Ranulf's interactions away from the historical events must have added at least 200 pages of padding.<br /><br />I also wasn't keen on certain aspects of the book's structure. There was a repeated style of scene where characters are discussing the events of the day and then someone bursts in, either with a message or to announce the arrival of a messenger. This was repeated so often I came to expect it whenever people were sitting down having a discussion. It made for a certain staleness and sense of deja vu. There were also quite a few places where someone explains all about something or someone to another character in an extended infodump, quite often done between made up characters who only appear for that purpose.<br /><br />I also appreciate that there were a lot of characters in the real history, and many had the same or similar names, but it did get quite confusing at times and I just couldn't remember who someone from among the minor characters was, especially if they had been out of the picture for a few chapters. The list of characters at the start of the book only lists the main ones plus Ranulf and his invented friends and relations.<br /><br />These issues made it a bit of a struggle to get through the book although I did persevere as I did want to know what happened and found the character of the future Henry II attractive. Therefore my overall rating balances out at 3 stars.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1832313741141072174" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_83764175" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83764175" />
    <a title="Moppet" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3118209-moppet"><img alt="Moppet" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262807428p2/3118209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/83764175?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Moppet" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Moppet" href="/user/show/3118209-moppet">Moppet</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/7031326-when-christ-and-his-saints-slept">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3118209-moppet?shelf=chunkster-challenge">chunkster-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3118209-moppet?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3118209-moppet?shelf=medieval">medieval</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3118209-moppet?shelf=12th-century">12th-century</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83764175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8749518046673700391">When I was a little girl I had a chart showing the Kings and Queens of England on my bedroom wall. I was especially interested in the Queens of England - that is, the ones who had ruled in their own right, not the consorts. But there weren't too many of those. Prior to Mary I (if you don't count Lady Jane Grey), there was only one - Matilda.<br/><br/>So I was disappointed to learn that Matilda had never really reigned. On his death her father, Henry I, who had lost his only legitimate son in the wreck of </span>
  <span id="freeText8749518046673700391" style="display:none">When I was a little girl I had a chart showing the Kings and Queens of England on my bedroom wall. I was especially interested in the Queens of England - that is, the ones who had ruled in their own right, not the consorts. But there weren't too many of those. Prior to Mary I (if you don't count Lady Jane Grey), there was only one - Matilda.<br /><br />So I was disappointed to learn that Matilda had never really reigned. On his death her father, Henry I, who had lost his only legitimate son in the wreck of the White Ship, left the crown to her. But her cousin Stephen seized the throne, beginning a civil war of nearly twenty years (1135-1154), a period of misrule, bloodshed and suffering when, as the Peterborough Chronicle put it, 'Christ and all his saints slept.'<br /><br />Sharon Kay Penman follows the main protagonists - Matilda herself (here called Maude, the vernacular version of her name, because Stephen was also married to a Matilda), her estranged husband Geoffrey of Anjou, Stephen and his wife Matilda of Boulogne - untangling the complex intrigues of the time and providing glimpses of the effects of the war on the unfortunate peasants and townspeople who were caught up in the conflict. She also follows the fortunes of a fictional character, Ranulf, illegitimate son of Henry I, who decides to support his half-sister Maude, but at great personal cost.<br /><br />Ranulf's adventures provide a link between the first two thirds of the book - the conflict between Maude and Stephen - and the last third, when the next generation reignites the war all over again. Stephen wants to crown his son Eustace king in his lifetime, while Maude and Geoffrey are determined that their son Henry, already Duke of Normandy, will win the crown of England. Although this book and its sequels, Time and Chance and Devil's Brood, are sometimes called the 'Eleanor of Aquitaine trilogy', Eleanor herself doesn't make an appearance until 700 pages in. When she does, sparks immediately fly between her and Henry, despite the fact that she is still - unhappily - married to the King of France.<br /><br />For me personally, this was an excellent introduction to a period of English history I didn't know much about and a chance to meet two fascinating twelfth-century women, the Empress Maude and Eleanor of Aquitaine. There was just one thing about the book which disappointed me - we don't get to meet Henry I, whose actions are the catalyst for much of the plot. I wanted to know more about him and his relationship with Maude/Matilda. <br /><br />There are some books which leave you feeling glad that you read them, sorry you've come to the end and exhilarated by the whole experience. This is one of them.<br /><br />I've quoted from my two favourite scenes on my blog.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://misadventuresofmoppet.wordpress.com/2010/04/02/a-tale-of-two-queens-when-christ-and-his-saints-slept-by-sharon-kay-penman/">http://misadventuresofmoppet.wordpres...</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8749518046673700391" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8Gb6noK57FEGE1ANanfjcEKpzzgcjzduu5bCeUK6tFteAjci/t/pZc7xqifFvZvfkZthfH0pvGgyG7Er61cH7A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0Nyr0K24nmqygB6oX9+IgNovTOD+FnM9vEge+boe6hJ+uGZs0d6bXnpi5ILwFfAvCR3ipJ+w+Ds1xW2rE/NZpQ==')})
  }

Sur<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText845637130590886771\" style=\"display:none\">She became Queen of Scots when she was only six days old. Life among the warring factions in Scotland was dangerous for the infant Queen, however, and at age five Mary was sent to France to be raised alongside her betrothed, the Dauphin Francois. Surrounded by all the sensual comforts of the French court, Mary\'s youth was peaceful, charmed, and when she became Queen of France at the age of sixteen, she seemed to have all she could wish for. But by her eighteenth birthday, Mary was a widow who had lost one throne and had been named by the Pope for another. And her extraordinary adventure had only begun. Defying her powerful cousin Elizabeth I, Mary set sail in 1561 to take her place as the Catholic Queen of a newly Protestant Scotland. A virtual stranger in her volatile native land, Mary would be hailed as a saint, denounced as a whore, and ultimately accused of murdering her second husband, Lord Darnley, in order to marry her lover, the Earl of Bothwell. She was but twenty-five years old when she fled Scotland for the imagined sanctuary of Elizabeth\'s England, where she would be embroiled in intrigue until she was beheaded &quot;like a criminal&quot; in 1587. In her stunning first novel, The Autobiography of Henry VIII, Margaret George established herself as one of the finest historical novelists of our time. Now she brings us a new, mesmerizing blend of history and storytelling as she turns the astonishing facts of the life of Mary Queen of Scots into magnificent fiction that sweeps us from the glittering French court where Mary spent her youth, to the bloodstained Scotland where she reigned as Queen, to the cold English castles where she ended her days. The son of William’s chamberlain, he shares a special bond with Waltheof, who rescued him from being trampled by a horse when he was a squire. Now Simon enjoys the confidence of both the King and the rebel earl.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/24655.Sharon_Kay_Penman">About Sharon Kay Penman</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/24655.Sharon_Kay_Penman"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1234237583p3/24655.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/24655.Sharon_Kay_Penman">Sharon Kay Penman
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
3,429
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9994138285355869139">Penman received her bachelor's degree from the University of Texas at Austin, she majored in history, and also received a Juris Doctor (J.D.) degree from Rutgers University School of Law, and later worked as a tax lawyer. <br/><br/>The Sunne in Splendour, a novel about Richard III of England is one of the most popular books on the Historical Novel Society's list of best historical novels. In 1996, following</span>
  <span id="freeText9994138285355869139" style="display:none">Penman received her bachelor's degree from the University of Texas at Austin, she majored in history, and also received a Juris Doctor (J.D.) degree from Rutgers University School of Law, and later worked as a tax lawyer. <br /><br />The Sunne in Splendour, a novel about Richard III of England is one of the most popular books on the Historical Novel Society's list of best historical novels. In 1996, following the success of When Christ and His Saints Slept (which dealt with the Anarchy and the early career of King Henry II of England), Penman ventured into the historical whodunnit with four mysteries set in the court of Eleanor of Aquitaine during the reign of Richard I. The mysteries did not enjoy the same success as her "straight" historical novels, to which she returned in 2002, with Time and Chance, again covering the life of Eleanor of Aquitaine and Henry II. In 2008, she published Devil's Brood, which was to be the final book in her trilogy about Henry II and Eleanor of Aquitaine. She soon realized that there was still more of the Angevins' story to tell and the result was Lionheart , followed by The King's Ransom. Henry and Eleanor's celebrated and controversial son, Richard the Lionheart is the major character in both books, although Eleanor, John, and Richard's favorite sister, Joanna, also get to spend time on center stage. She has just finished The Land Beyond the Sea, set in the Kingdom of Jerusalem in the late 12th century. It will be published in the U.S. by G.P. Putnam's and in the U.K. and Down Under by Macmillan and co; the publication date is early March, 2020. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9994138285355869139" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

Where the second novel in the trilogy, Time And Chanc<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText5788193659108007402\" style=\"display:none\">The long-awaited and highly anticipated final volume in Penman’s trilogy of Henry II and Eleanor of Aquitaine—a tumultuous conclusion to this timeless story of love, power, ambition, and betrayal. Where the second novel in the trilogy, Time And Chance, dealt with the extraordinary politics of the twelfth century, climaxing with the murder of Thomas Becket and Henry’s confrontation with the Church and self-imposed exile to Ireland, Devil’s Brood centers on the implosion of a family. And because it is a royal family whose domains span the English Channel and whose alliances encompass the Christian world, that collapse will have dire consequences. This is a story of betrayal as Henry’s three eldest sons and his wife enter into a rebellion against him, aligning themselves with his bitterest enemy, King Louis of France. But it is also the story of a great king whose brilliance forged an empire but whose personal blind spots led him into the most serious mistake of his life. Sharon Kay Penman has created a novel of tremendous power, as two strong-willed, passionate people clash, a family divides, and a marriage ends in all but name. Curiously, it is a novel without villains—only flawed human beings caught up in misperceptions and bad judgment calls. Most devastating to Henry was not his sons’ rebellion but his wife’s betrayal in joining them. How could it happen that two people whose love for each other was all consuming end up as bitter adversaries?             if ($('bookCover_2859559').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_2859559').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
